% Ans        : ShortAns
% File       : 0031
% Sub        : Related-Rates
% Topic      : Derivative
% Type       : Compute

\ProblemFileHeader{493}
\ifquestionPull
\ifproblemToFind\latexProblemContent{
\ifVerboseLocation This is Derivative Compute Question 0031. \\ \fi
\begin{problem}

A road running north to south crosses a road going east to west at the point $P$.  Cyclist $A$ is riding north along the first road, and cyclist $B$ is riding east along the second road.  At a particular time, cyclist $A$ is $96$ miles to the north of $P$ and traveling at $25$ miles per hour, while cyclist $B$ is $180$ miles to the east of $P$ and traveling at $\frac{40}{3}$ miles per hour.  How fast is the distance between the two cyclists changing? \\[0.5in]

\input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{\frac{400}{17}}$ miles per hour.
\end{problem}}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\latexProblemContent{
\ifVerboseLocation This is Derivative Compute Question 0031. \\ \fi
\begin{problem}

A road running north to south crosses a road going east to west at the point $P$.  Cyclist $A$ is riding north along the first road, and cyclist $B$ is riding east along the second road.  At a particular time, cyclist $A$ is $42$ kilometers to the north of $P$ and traveling at $12$ kilometers per hour, while cyclist $B$ is $56$ kilometers to the east of $P$ and traveling at $9$ kilometers per hour.  How fast is the distance between the two cyclists changing? \\[0.5in]

\input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{\frac{72}{5}}$ kilometers per hour.
\end{problem}}

At a particular time, cyclist $A$ is $96$ miles to the north of $P$ and traveling at $45$ miles per hour, while cyclist $B$ is $180$ miles to the east of $P$ and traveling at $24$ miles per hour.  How fast is the distance between the two cyclists changing? \\[0.5in]

\input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{\frac{720}{17}}$ miles per hour.
\end{problem}}

\end{problem}}

\ifVerboseLocation This is Derivative Compute Question 0031. \\ \fi
\begin{problem}

A road running north to south crosses a road going east to west at the point $P$.  Cyclist $A$ is riding north along the first road, and cyclist $B$ is riding east along the second road.  At a particular time, cyclist $A$ is $35$ kilometers to the north of $P$ and traveling at $24$ kilometers per hour, while cyclist $B$ is $84$ kilometers to the east of $P$ and traveling at $10$ kilometers per hour.  How fast is the distance between the two cyclists changing? \\[0.5in]

\input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{\frac{240}{13}}$ kilometers per hour.
\end{problem}}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\latexProblemContent{
\ifVerboseLocation This is Derivative Compute Question 0031. \\ \fi
\begin{problem}

A road running north to south crosses a road going east to west at the point $P$.  Cyclist $A$ is riding north along the first road, and cyclist $B$ is riding east along the second road. How fast is the distance between the two cyclists changing? \\[0.5in]

\input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{\frac{600}{13}}$ kilometers per hour.
\end{problem}}

How fast is the distance between the two cyclists changing? \\[0.5in]

\input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{\frac{48}{5}}$ kilometers per hour.
\end{problem}}

At a particular time, cyclist $A$ is $33$ miles to the north of $P$ and traveling at $20$ miles per hour, while cyclist $B$ is $44$ miles to the east of $P$ and traveling at $15$ miles per hour.  How fast is the distance between the two cyclists changing? \\[0.5in]

\input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{24}$ miles per hour.
\end{problem}}

How fast is the distance between the two cyclists changing? \\[0.5in]

\input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{24}$ kilometers per hour.
\end{problem}}

\ifVerboseLocation This is Derivative Compute Question 0031. \\ \fi
\begin{problem}

A road running north to south crosses a road going east to west at the point $P$.  Cyclist $A$ is riding north along the first road, and cyclist $B$ is riding east along the second road.  At a particular time, cyclist $A$ is $6$ miles to the north of $P$ and traveling at $8$ miles per hour, while cyclist $B$ is $8$ miles to the east of $P$ and traveling at $6$ miles per hour.  How fast is the distance between the two cyclists changing? \\[0.5in]

\input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{\frac{48}{5}}$ miles per hour.
\end{problem}}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\latexProblemContent{
\ifVerboseLocation This is Derivative Compute Question 0031. \\ \fi
\begin{problem}

At a particular time, cyclist $A$ is $15$ miles to the north of $P$ and traveling at $8$ miles per hour, while cyclist $B$ is $20$ miles to the east of $P$ and traveling at $6$ miles per hour. \input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{\frac{48}{5}}$ miles per hour.
\end{problem}}

\ifVerboseLocation This is Derivative Compute Question 0031. \\ \fi
\begin{problem}

A road running north to south crosses a road going east to west at the point $P$.  Cyclist $A$ is riding north along the first road, and cyclist $B$ is riding east along the second road.  At a particular time, cyclist $A$ is $21$ thousand feet to the north of $P$ and traveling at $20$ feet per second, while cyclist $B$ is $28$ thousand feet to the east of $P$ and traveling at $15$ feet per second.  How fast is the distance between the two cyclists changing? \\[0.5in]

\input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{24}$ feet per second.
\end{problem}}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\latexProblemContent{
\ifVerboseLocation This is Derivative Compute Question 0031. \\ \fi
\begin{problem}

A road running north to south crosses a road going east to west at the point $P$.  Cyclist $A$ is riding north along the first road, and cyclist $B$ is riding east along the second road.  At a particular time, cyclist $A$ is $18$ hundred meters to the north of $P$ and traveling at $8$ meters per second, while cyclist $B$ is $24$ hundred meters to the east of $P$ and traveling at $6$ meters per second.  How fast is the distance between the two cyclists changing? \\[0.5in]

\input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{\frac{48}{5}}$ meters per second.
\end{problem}}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{\frac{540}{13}}$ feet per second.
\end{problem}}

At a particular time, cyclist $A$ is $60$ miles to the north of $P$ and traveling at $24$ miles per hour, while cyclist $B$ is $144$ miles to the east of $P$ and traveling at $10$ miles per hour.  How fast is the distance between the two cyclists changing? \\[0.5in]

\input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{\frac{240}{13}}$ miles per hour.
\end{problem}}

\input{Derivative-Compute-0031.HELP.tex}

The distance between the two cyclists is increasing by $\answer{\frac{240}{17}}$ kilometers per hour.
\end{problem}}
